Judge Must Not Host One Litigant Without the Other
Ruling with hadith proofs on judge's hospitality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge hosting one litigant alone and identify the hadith proofs that establish this prohibition.

Core Idea
A judge must not host one litigant without the other — it creates suspicion of bias.

Justice in the courtroom begins before the verdict. The judge's conduct must be above reproach, ensuring no party feels disadvantaged. This lesson examines a specific ruling: a judge may not extend private hospitality to one litigant without the other. From the hadith of Umm Salama, Ibn al-Zubayr, and the practice of 'Ali, the Hanafi school derives a clear prohibition. You will learn the textual proofs and the underlying rationale of avoiding bias.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What specific action is being ruled upon? (Answer: A judge inviting only one of two litigants to a meal). What is the hukm? (Answer: Makruh tahrimi – prohibited).
The ruling applies only when there is an ongoing case between the litigants.
2
Locate the Dalil
The text cites three hadith. List them: (1) Umm Salama's hadith on equity in glance, gesture, and seating. (2) Ibn al-Zubayr's hadith that both litigants sit before the judge. (3) The hadith of 'Ali: the Prophet forbade hosting a litigant without his opponent.
All three hadith are ahad (solitary), but their meanings are clear (qati' al-dalala).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does each hadith prove the ruling? For (1): command to be equal implies prohibition of favoring one. For (2): seating both equally shows no preference. For (3): explicit prohibition of hosting one litigant alone.
The prohibition is derived directly from the explicit text (nass) in the third hadith.
4
Note the Scope and Application
Does the ruling apply to all hospitality? Only when a case is pending. If the judge invites both or if no case exists, it is permissible. The rationale is avoiding suspicion of partiality.
Some scholars extend it to any form of favoritism, but the text limits it to hospitality.

[۲۹۰۲] (۱۵) ولا يضيف احد الخصمين دون خصمه [۲۹۰۲] (۱۵) اور نہ مہمان نوازی کرے ضمین میں تنہا ایک کی۔ قاضی کے پاس دو آدمیوں کا مقدمہ چل رہا ہو تو ان میں سے ایک کی دعوت کرے اور ایک کی نہ کرے ایسا نہ کرے۔ دعوت کرے تو دونوں کی کرے۔ ایک کی طرف میلان سے شبہ ہوتا ہے کہ فیصلہ میں اس کی رعایت کی جائے گی۔ اس لئے ایک کی دعوت کرنا اچھا نہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ام سلمة قالت قال رسول الله الا الله من ابتلى بالقضاء بين الناس فليعدل بينهم في لحظه و اشارته ومقعده (الف) (دار قطنی کتاب فی الاقضية والاحکام، ج رابع ، ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۴۴۲۰ رسنن بیہقی ، باب انصاف الصمين في المدخل عليه والاستماع منهما میں ، حجته وحسن الاقبال عليهما ، ج عاشر ص ۲۲۸، نمبر ۲۰۴۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دونوں حضمین کے درمیان لحظے میں ۔ اشارے اور بٹھانے میں برابری کرے (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن الزبير قال: قضى رسول الله الله ان الخصمين يقعد ان بين يدى الحكم (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب کیف مجلس بین یدی القاضی، ص، نمبر ۳۵۸۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دونوں شخصموں کو برابر بٹھائے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کسی ایک کو ترجیح نہ دے (۴) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن الحسن قال نزل على على رجل وهو بالكوفة ثم قدم خصما له فقال له على اخصم انت؟ قال نعم ، قال فتحول فان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلمه نهانا ان نضيف الخصم الا وخصمه معه (ج) (سن للبیہقی ، باب لا ينبغي للقاضي ان يضيف الخصم الا وخصمه معہ، ج عاشر ص ۲۳۲ نمبره ۲۰۴۷) اس حدیث میں صاف ہے کہ ایک مقصم کی دعوت نہ کرے۔
[2902] (15) He should not host one of the two litigants without his opponent. He should not invite only one of them if a case is ongoing between them. If he invites, he should invite both. Inviting only one creates suspicion that the judge may favor him in the verdict. Therefore, it is not good to invite one. (2) In a hadith: Umm Salama said the Prophet said: 'Whoever is tried with judging between people should be equitable between them in his glance, gesture, and seating.' (al-Daraqutni, Chapter on Judgments, vol. 4, p. 131, no. 4420; al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Fairness to Two Opponents, vol. 10, p. 228, no. 20457) From this hadith it is learned that he should be equal between the two litigants in glance, gesture, and seating. (3) In a hadith: Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr said: The Prophet decreed that the two litigants should sit before the judge. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on How to Sit Before the Judge, no. 3588) This hadith shows that both should sit equally. (4) In a hadith: al-Hasan said: 'Ali hosted a man while he was in Kufa; then his opponent came. 'Ali said to him: 'Are you the opponent?' He said yes. He said: 'Move aside, for the Prophet forbade us from hosting a litigant unless his opponent is with him.' (al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Judge Not to Host One Litigant Without His Opponent, vol. 10, p. 232, no. 20477) This hadith clearly states not to invite one litigant alone.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that a judge must not extend hospitality (like inviting for a meal) to only one of two litigants in a case before him. Doing so creates a strong presumption of bias and favoritism. The text provides multiple hadith to support this: the hadith of Umm Salama commands equality in glance, gesture, and seating; the hadith of Ibn al-Zubayr says both must sit before the judge; and the hadith of 'Ali explicitly shows the Prophet's prohibition of hosting one litigant without the other. The ruling applies to private hospitality; if the judge invites both together, it is permissible.

Key Terms
يضيف (yudīf): To host or invite to a meal as hospitality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is recommended as strengthening ties
B) It is permissible if the meal is simple
C) It is prohibited because it shows bias
D) It is neutral and left to the judge's discretion

Key Takeaway
A judge must never extend private hospitality to one litigant alone, as it undermines the appearance of impartiality.

The Judge's Duty of Equality: Seating, Attention, and Prohibition of Favoritism
Ruling on equal treatment of litigants in seating and attention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state at least four specific actions a judge must avoid to ensure equality between litigants, and identify the underlying proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
A judge must treat both litigants equally in every visible aspect — seating, attention, whispering, greeting, gestures.

In Islamic court proceedings, the judge's impartiality is paramount. This lesson examines a clear ruling from the Hanafi tradition on how a judge must behave when both litigants are present. The ruling extends beyond mere seating to include eye contact, gestures, and even private whispers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge's conduct when both litigants are present. The ruling is that the judge must treat them equally (wajib).
The ruling is based on a hadith commanding equality.
2
List the specific requirements
From the text, enumerate: equal seating, equal attention, no whispering to one, no special greeting, no inclination or gesture.
3
Connect to the proof
The hadith quoted in the commentary: 'Let him be equitable between them in his glance, gesture, and seat.' The imperative indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
Hadith source: al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that equality is wajib with no intra-madhhab difference. It is agreed upon across schools.
Cross-madhhab status: muttafaq alayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۰۳](١۶) فاذا حضرا سوى بينهما في الجلوس والاقبال ولا يسارر احدا ولا يخصه بالتحية ولا بميل ولا بغم[؟] فاذا قضى بينهم رفع [۲۹۰۳] (۱۲) پس جب دونوں حاضر ہوں تو برابری کرے بیٹھنے میں متوجہ کرنے میں اور سرگوشی نہ کرے کسی ایک سے اور نہ اس کی طرف متوجہ ہو سلام میں اور نہ میلان سے اور نہ اشارہ سے۔ پس جب فیصلہ کرے تو اٹھے۔
[2903] (16) When both present, he should make them equal in seating and attention, and should not whisper to one, nor single him out with greeting, nor with inclination, nor with gesture[?]. When he judges between them, he should rise.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage details the requirement of complete impartiality when both litigants are present before the judge. The judge must ensure they sit equally, give them equal attention, avoid whispering to one, avoid greeting one specially, and avoid any physical inclination or gesture that might indicate favoritism. After rendering judgment, the judge should rise (presumably to leave the court or to end the session). This ruling is based on the hadith of Umm Salama mentioned earlier, which commands equality in glance, gesture, and seating. The prohibition of whispering is also implied in that hadith.

Key Terms
يسارر (yusārir): To whisper to someone, especially out of earshot of others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He may greet one first if he knows him
B) He should make them sit equally and not whisper to either
C) He may speak to one privately if he needs clarification
D) He may favor the one who came first

Key Takeaway
A judge must ensure complete parity between litigants in all visible aspects, from seating to gestures, to uphold the integrity of the court.

The Judge's Duty of Impartiality in Behavior
Ruling with proof on judicial impartiality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited behaviors for a judge and explain why each is wajib based on the hadith.

Core Idea
A judge must be impartial even in glance, gesture, and seating—appearance of justice is wajib.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri addresses a crucial aspect of Islamic judicial ethics: the judge's conduct must not only be fair in judgment but also appear fair in every physical action. The ruling is binding (wajib) and is supported by a clear hadith from the Prophet ﷺ. In this lesson, we will unpack the three explicit prohibitions and understand the legal reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibitions
Read the Arabic matn: 'yusār aḥadahumā wa lā yushīru ilayhi wa lā yulaqqinuhu ḥujjah'. Identify each prohibition and its meaning: whispering, gesturing, and teaching an argument.
These are all actions that suggest partiality to one litigant.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Umm Salamah (radiyallahu 'anha) recorded by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi. Identify the chain and the text.
The hadith explicitly mentions 'glance, gesture, and seat'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyadil' (let him be just) in Hanafi usul indicates wujub (obligation). The specification of three physical aspects shows that impartiality extends beyond the verdict.
The law is derived from the explicit command in the hadith.
4
Note the consensus
The Hanafi position is that this ruling is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh). There is no intra- or inter-madhhab dispute on this basic principle.
However, the application of what constitutes partiality may vary.
5
Apply to modern contexts
Think about how a judge in an Islamic court today must avoid even subtle biases, such as looking at one party more often or using a tone that favors one side.
The appearance of justice is part of justice itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسار احدهما ولا يشيرا اليه ولا يلقنه حجة
ان دونوں مدعی اور مدعی علیہ قاضی کے پاس حاضر ہوں تو قاضی کوئی ایسی حرکت نہ کرے جس سے محسوس ہو کہ یہ کسی ایک کی طرف مائل ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں کو برابر درجے میں بٹھائے۔ دونوں کی طرف برابر درجے میں متوجہ ہو۔ کسی ایک سے چپکے چپکے بات نہ کرے۔ کسی ایک کی طرف اشارہ نہ کرے۔ کسی ایک کو بچنے کی دلیل نہ بتائے۔
کیونکہ اس طرح انصاف کا تقاضا پورا نہیں ہو سکے گا (۲) او پر حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ عن ام سلمة قال قالت قال رسول الله من ابتلى بالقضاء بين الناس فليعدل بينهم في لحظه واشارته ومقعده (الف) (دار قطنی ،نمبر ۴۴۲۰ رسنن بیہقی ، نمبر ۲۰۴۵۷) سوئی : برابری کرے۔ لایسار : سر سے مشتق ہے، سرگوشی نہ کرے۔ ولا یلقنہ : تلقین سے مشتق ہے، کسی چیز کو بتانا ، دلائل سمجھانا
He should not whisper to one of them nor gesture to him nor teach him an argument. When both plaintiff and defendant are present before the judge, the judge should not do any action from which it is perceived that he is inclined towards one of them. Therefore, he should seat them in equal positions. He should turn to both equally. He should not whisper to one. He should not gesture to one. He should not teach one a defense. Because in this way the requirement of justice will not be fulfilled (2). A hadith has already passed: from Umm Salamah, she said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever is tried with judging between people, let him be just between them in his glance, his gesture, and his seat.' (al-Daraqutni, no. 4420; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, no. 20457). Suwi: treat equally. La yusar: derived from sirr, meaning do not whisper. Wa la yulaqqinuhu: derived from talqin, meaning to teach something, to explain arguments.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the judge's obligation of impartiality. The Arabic matn states three prohibitions: the judge must not whisper to one litigant, must not gesture to him, and must not teach him an argument. The Urdu commentary expands: both litigants must be seated at the same level, the judge must direct his attention equally to both, avoid private conversation, avoid any gesture that suggests bias, and avoid coaching one party on how to win his case. The reason given is that such actions undermine the appearance of justice. The proof is a hadith from Umm Salamah reported by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi, where the Prophet commands equality in glance, gesture, and seating. The commentary then glosses key terms: 'suwi' means equality, 'lā yusār' from sirr (secret) means no whispering, 'lā yulaqqinuhu' from talqīn means not teaching him arguments or suggestions. This ruling establishes that judicial impartiality is not merely about the final judgment but extends to every visible behavior in the courtroom.

Key Terms
يسار (yusār): Whispering or speaking secretly to one litigant, which suggests partiality.
يلقنه (yulaqqinuhu): Teaching or prompting a litigant with arguments or evidence to help his case.
سوي (suwī): Equality; treating both parties alike in all aspects of the court proceeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, in what three things must the judge be just between the litigants?
A) In speech, in writing, and in decision
B) In glance, in gesture, and in seat
C) In private consultation, in public statement, and in verdict
D) In wealth, in status, and in lineage

Key Takeaway
A judge must maintain outward impartiality in glance, gesture, and seat; any deviation risks violating the wajib command of the Prophet ﷺ.

Imprisonment of the Procrastinating Debtor in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on when a judge may imprison a debtor who delays payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on imprisoning a debtor who procrastinates, distinguish between cases where a substitute (badal) was received and cases where it was not, and apply the hadith evidence to justify the ruling.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is a penalty for procrastination (mumatala), not for inability; a debtor who received a substitute is presumed able to pay.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri explains the detailed rules regarding the imprisonment of a debtor who deliberately delays payment. The judge must not act hastily; instead, he must distinguish whether the debt is proven by confession or by witnesses, and whether the debtor received a substitute (badal) in exchange for the debt. Understanding this distinction ensures that imprisonment is applied only as a punishment for procrastination, not for genuine inability, thereby protecting the poor from unjust detention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge's imprisonment of a procrastinating debtor. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) only when the debtor has the means to pay but delays without excuse. The text emphasizes that imprisonment is a penalty for mumatala, not for inability.
Inability to pay does not warrant imprisonment; the judge must first order payment and give time.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof cited is the hadith: 'لَيُّ الْوَاجِدِ يُحِلُّ عِرْضَهُ وَعُقُوبَتَهُ' (The wealthy procrastinator makes his honor and punishment lawful). Also, the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) are mentioned.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operativeness of the dalil lies in the word 'al-wajid' (wealthy) and 'yahillu' (becomes lawful). 'Al-wajid' limits the ruling to those who have the means; 'yahillu' indicates permissibility of both harsh treatment (honor) and imprisonment (punishment). This shows that only a solvent procrastinator is liable, and the judge may imprison to compel payment.
Ibn al-Mubarak's explanation clarifies 'his honor becomes lawful' means to treat harshly, and 'his punishment' means imprisonment.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and key distinction
The passage distinguishes between debts where the debtor received a substitute (badal) in hand (e.g., price of sold item, loan amount, dower) and those where he did not (e.g., diyah for injury). In the former, the receipt of the substitute is itself evidence of ability to pay, so imprisonment is allowed even without separate proof of wealth. In the latter, investigation into the debtor's financial status is required first.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position; some other schools require explicit proof of wealth even when a substitute was received.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۱۲۹۰۴) فاذا ثبت الحق عنده وطلب صاحب الحق حبس غريمه لم يعجل بحبسه وامره بدفع ما عليه فان امتنع حبسه في كل اشارہ کرے، نہ کوئی حجت سکھائے۔
اقرار کے ذریعہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ مدعی علیہ پر حق ہے۔ اور مدعی درخواست کرتا ہے کہ فورا مدعی علیہ کو قید کیا جائے تو قاضی کو چاہئے کہ فورا اس کو قید نہ کرے بلکہ اس کو حکم دے کہ تم مدعی کا حق ادا کرو۔ اگر وہ ادا نہ کرے اور بغیر کسی عذر کے ٹال مٹول کرے تب قاضی کو اختیار ہے کہ اس کو قید کرے۔
قید کرنا ٹال مٹول کی سزا ہے۔ اور اقرار کرنے والا خود اقرار کرتا ہے کہ اتنی چیز میرے اوپر لازم ہے۔ اس لئے ممکن ہے کہ رقم ساتھ نہ لایا ہو اس لئے ابھی اس کا ٹال مٹول ظاہر نہیں ہوا۔ اس لئے ابھی قید نہ کرے۔ اتنی مہلت ضرور دے جس میں گھر جا کر وہ چیز لا کر دگی کے حوالے کر سکے۔ ٹال مثال ظاہر ہو تب ہی فید کرے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمر بن الشريد عن ابيه عن رسول الله الله قال: لى الواجد يحل عرضه وعقوبته، قال ابن المبارك يحل عرضه يغلظ له وعقوبته يحبس له (ب) دوسری رویت میں ہے۔
عن بهر بن حكيم عن ابيه عن جده ان النبي الا الله حبس رجلا في تهمته (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الدین هل تحبس به ، ج ۲، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۳۶۳۰/۳۶۲۸ / بخاری شریف، باب لصاحب الحق مقال ، ص ۳۲۳، نمبر ۲۴۰۱، کتاب ا؛ استقراض رالنسائی شریف، باب مطل الغنی ص ۶۴۵ نمبر ۴۶۹۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ٹال مٹول کرے تو اس کو جبس یعنی قید کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جو لوگوں کے درمیان قضا میں مبتلا ہو تو وہ دیکھنے میں اشارے میں اور بیٹھنے میں انصاف کرے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جس کے پاس مال ہے پھر بھی ٹال مٹول کرے تو اس کی عزت اور سزا حلال ہے۔ ابن مبارک نے فرمایا کہ اس کی عزت حلال ہے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ حتی کرے اور اس کی سزا کا مطلب یہ ہے اس کو قید کرے ( ج ) آپ نے تہت میں ایک آدمی کو قید کیا۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع
۱۸۷
کتاب آداب القاضی)
دين لزمه بدلا عن مال حصل في يده كثمن المبيع وبدل القرض [۲۹۰۵ (۱۸) او التزمه بعقد كالمهر والكفالة.
گواہوں کے ذریعہ کسی پر حق ثابت ہو جائے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ کافی دیر سے مدعی علیہ ٹال مٹول کر رہا تھا۔ آخر گواہ کے ذریعہ حق ثابت کیا گیا اس لئے فورا حبس کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ حقوق دو قسم کے ہیں۔ ایک تو وہ جس کے بدلے میں مدعی علیہ کے ہاتھ میں رقم وغیرہ آئی ہے جیسے بیع کی قیمت کا دعوی ہو تو مدعی علیہ کے ہاتھ میں مبیع آئی ہے جس کی قیمت ادا کرنی ہے یا مہر اس کے بدلے میں بضعہ آیا ہے۔ یا قرض کا مطالبہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کے ہاتھ میں قرض کی رقم آئی ہے۔ ان سب صورتوں میں مدعی کے ہاتھ میں مطالبے کا بدلہ آیا ہوا ہے پھر بھی وہ اس کا عوض نہیں دینا چاہتا۔ ایسی صورتوں میں مدعی علیہ غریب ہو یا مالدار اس کو جبس کیا جائے گا۔
اس کے ہاتھ میں بدل آنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ وہ عوض دے سکتا ہے تب ہی تو اس نے مثلا طبیع خریدا، قرض لیا یا شادی کی (۲) اوپر جو حدیث گزری۔ (لى الواجد يحل عرضه وعقوبته ) اس میں فرمایا کہ مال پانے والے کے ٹال متول کی سزا یہ ہے کہ اس کی عزت بھی حلال ہے یعنی برا بھلا کہہ سکتے ہو اور اس کی سزا بھی حلال ہے یعنی جس کر سکتے ہو۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال پانے والا ہو تو اس کو قید کر سکتے ہو۔ اور اگر ابھی فوری طور پر مال نہیں ملا ہے مثل کسی کا ہاتھ کا نا جس کی دیت ایک ہزار درہم دینے ہے تو ہاتھ کے بدلے میں قاطع کو بھی کچھ نہیں ملا ہے تو یہ ابھی مال کا پانے والا نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کو ابھی جس نہیں کریں گے بلکہ تحقیق کے بعد معلوم ہو جائے کہ اس کے پاس دیست ادا کرنے کے لئے مال ہے پھر بھی ٹال مٹول کر رہا ہے تب جبس کریں گے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن جابر عن الشعبي قال: الحبس في الـديـن حـيـلـة قـال وقال جابر كان على يحبس في الدين (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الحبس فی الدین، ج ثامن، ص ۳۰۶ نمبر ۱۵۳۱۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ دین میں اور قرض میں جس فرماتے تھے۔ اور اسی میں وہ تمام صورتیں داخل ہوں گی جس میں مدعی علیہ کو بدلہ مل گیا ہو۔
جس : قید کرے جس کرے۔ فریم : مقروض۔ [۲۹۰۵] (۱۸) یا اس کو عقد کے ذریعہ لازم کیا ہو جیسے مہر اور کفالہ۔
سکے گا۔
شادی کی جس کی وجہ سے مہر لازم ہوا۔ اگر مہر دینے میں ٹال مٹول ظاہر ہوا تو گواہ کے ذریعہ مالدار ہونا ثابت نہ بھی ہو پھر بھی جبس کیا جا
مہر بضعہ کا بدلہ ہے۔ مدعی علیہ کے ہاتھ میں بضعہ آیا جس کے بدلے میں مہر معجل دینا پڑے گا ارنہ دینے پر قید کیا جائے گا (۲) نکاح پر اقدام کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کے پاس مال ہے۔ اگر مہر متقبل دینے کی بھی استطاعت نہیں تھی تو شادی کا اقدام کیوں کیا؟ اس لئے اس میں ٹال مٹول کرنے پر جبس کیا جائے گا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علی دین میں قید کرتے تھے۔
[2904] When the truth is established in his view and the right-holder asks for the imprisonment of his debtor, he should not hasten to imprison him, and he should order him to pay what is upon him. If he refuses, he imprisons him in every... he should not gesture, nor teach any argument. When it is established through confession that the defendant owes a right, and the plaintiff requests that the defendant be immediately imprisoned, the judge should not immediately imprison him, but should order him: 'Pay the plaintiff's right.' If he does not pay and procrastinates without excuse, then the judge has the authority to imprison him. Imprisonment is the punishment for procrastination. And the one who confesses confesses that a certain thing is binding upon him. Therefore, it is possible that he did not bring the money with him, so his procrastination is not yet apparent. Thus, he should not imprison him immediately. He should give him sufficient time to go home, bring the thing, and hand it over to the [judge?]. Only when procrastination becomes evident should he imprison him. The proof of this is the hadith: from 'Amr ibn al-Sharid from his father from the Messenger of Allah, he said: 'The wealthy procrastinator makes his honor and his punishment lawful.' Ibn al-Mubarak said: 'His honor becomes lawful means to treat him harshly, and his punishment means to imprison him.' (b) In another narration: from Bahz ibn Hakim from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet (PBUH) imprisoned a man on suspicion. (c) (Abu Dawud, chapter on debt, vol. 2, p. 155, no. 3630/3628; Bukhari, chapter on the right-holder's statement, p. 323, no. 2401; al-Nasa'i, chapter on the procrastination of the wealthy, p. 645, no. 4693). From this hadith it is understood that if he procrastinates, he can be imprisoned, i.e., jailed. Footnote: (a) He said: Whoever is tried with judging between people, let him be just in his glance, gesture, and seat. (b) He said: The one who has wealth yet procrastinates, his honor and punishment are lawful. Ibn al-Mubarak said: 'His honor is lawful' means to treat him harshly, and 'his punishment' means to imprison him. (c) He imprisoned a man on suspicion. [PAGE_194] Al Sharh al-Thamiri vol. 4, p. 187, Kitab Adab al-Qadi: A debt that is binding as a substitute for property that came into his hand, like the price of a sold item and the substitute for a loan [2905] (18) or that which is undertaken by a contract like dower and guarantee. When a right is established against someone by witnesses, that means the defendant has been procrastinating for a long time. Finally, the right is established by witnesses, so if the judge wishes to imprison immediately, he can do so. Rights are of two types: one for which the defendant received money or something in his hand, like a claim for the price of a sale: the defendant received the sold item, whose price he must pay; or dower: in its place he received the vulva; or a demand for a loan: the defendant received the loan amount. In all these cases, the plaintiff's hand has received the substitute for the demand, yet he does not want to give its equivalent. In such cases, whether the defendant is poor or wealthy, he will be imprisoned. The fact that the substitute came into his hand is evidence that he can pay the substitute; otherwise, why would he have purchased, borrowed, or married? (2) The hadith that passed above: 'The wealthy procrastinator makes his honor and punishment lawful.' In it he said: The punishment for one who has wealth and procrastinates is that his honor is lawful, meaning you can speak ill of him, and his punishment is lawful, meaning you can imprison him. From this it is understood that if he has wealth, he can be imprisoned. And if he has not yet received the money immediately, like a hand cut off, for which the diyah is one thousand dirhams: the cutter did not receive anything in exchange for the hand, so he is not yet one who has wealth. Therefore, he will not be imprisoned immediately; rather, after investigation, if it becomes clear that he has wealth to pay the diyah but still procrastinates, then he will be imprisoned. (2) There is an athar: from Jabir from al-Sha'bi, he said: 'Imprisonment for debt is a trick.' He said: And Jabir said: 'Ali used to imprison for debt.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on imprisonment for debt, vol. 8, p. 306, no. 15312). This athar indicates that they used to imprison for debt and loan. And it includes all those cases where the defendant has received a substitute. Jass: imprison. Farim: debtor. [2905] (18) Or that which is made binding by contract like dower and guarantee. He can do so. Because of marriage, dower becomes binding. If procrastination becomes apparent in paying dower, even if his wealth is not established by witnesses, he will still be imprisoned. Dower is the substitute for the vulva; the defendant received the vulva, in exchange for which he must pay the prompt dower; if he does not pay, he will be imprisoned. (2) Undertaking marriage is evidence that the defendant has wealth. If he did not have the ability to pay the deferred dower, why would he have undertaken marriage? Therefore, if he procrastinates, he will be imprisoned. Footnote: (a) 'Ali used to imprison for debt.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the judge's authority to imprison a debtor who procrastinates in payment. The initial ruling distinguishes between two modes of proof: if the right is established by confession (iqrar), the judge should not immediately imprison; he must first order payment and give time sufficient for the debtor to bring the money. Imprisonment is only for procrastination (mumatala), not inability. If the right is established by witnesses, that indicates prolonged delay, so immediate imprisonment is permissible. The commentary then categorizes debts: those where the debtor received a substitute (badal) in his hand—like sale price (thaman mabi'), loan (qard), dower (mahr), and guarantee (kafalah)—and those where he did not, like diyah for injury. In the first category, the debtor's receipt of the substitute is evidence of his ability to pay, so imprisonment is allowed even if his wealth is not independently proven. In the second category, investigation into his wealth is needed first. The proofs include the hadith 'lay al-wajid yahillu 'irduhu wa 'uqubatuhu' (the wealthy procrastinator makes his honor and punishment lawful), the Prophet's imprisonment of a man on suspicion, and the practice of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib who imprisoned for debt. The footnote (b) explains the hadith: dishonor means harsh treatment, and punishment means imprisonment. The ruling establishes that imprisonment is a penalty for procrastination, not for inability to pay.

Key Terms
لي الواجد (lay al-wājid): Procrastination of a wealthy person; deliberately delaying payment despite having the means.
بدل (badal): Substitute or consideration received in exchange for a debt, e.g., the sold item for the price, the loaned amount, the vulva for dower.
حبس (habs): Imprisonment; legal detention as a penalty for procrastinating in payment of a debt.
مطل (muṭl): Delaying or procrastinating payment of a due debt without valid excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, when may a judge imprison a debtor immediately after proof of the debt?
A) Only when the debt is proven by confession.
B) When the debt is proven by witnesses and the debtor received a substitute (badal).
C) Only when the debtor is explicitly proven wealthy by independent evidence.
D) In all cases where a debt is due and the debtor is present.

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment for debt in Hanafi fiqh is a penalty for procrastination; the judge must distinguish cases where the debtor received a substitute, as that presumes ability to pay.

Imprisonment When Substitute Received for Debt
Explains when a debtor who received a substitute can be imprisoned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule regarding imprisonment for debt by identifying when a substitute (badal) has been received and stating the evidence.

Core Idea
Immediate imprisonment for debt is allowed if the debtor received a substitute (badal), indicating ability to pay.

This passage examines a key principle in Islamic legal procedure: the judge's discretion to imprison a debtor. The Hanafi school distinguishes between debts where the debtor received a substitute (e.g., price of sale, loan, mahr) and other debts. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, proof, and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of rights
Read the passage and note the distinction: rights with substitute (badal) and rights without. Examples: price of sale, loan amount, mahr.
The substitute is the wealth or benefit that came into the defendant's hands.
2
Examine the proof (hadith)
Analyze the hadith 'Al-wajid yahillu irdahu wa uqubatahu.' Understand that 'punishment' here includes imprisonment.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and is zanni al-thubut.
3
Contrast cases with and without substitute
Compare the loan case (substitute received) with diyah (no substitute). Note that diyah requires proof of wealth before imprisonment.
The absence of badal means the defendant is not automatically considered able to pay.
4
Recognize judicial discretion
The passage states 'if the judge wishes to imprison immediately, he may.' This is a discretionary power, not an obligation.
The hukm level is mubah (permissible).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دين لزمه بدلا عن مال حصل في يده كثمن المبيع وبدل القرض [۲۹۰۵ (۱۸) او التزمه بعقد كالمهر والكفالة. گواہوں کے ذریعہ کسی پر حق ثابت ہو جائے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ کافی دیر سے مدعی علیہ ٹال مٹول کر رہا تھا۔ آخر گواہ کے ذریعہ حق ثابت کیا گیا اس لئے فورا حبس کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ حقوق دو قسم کے ہیں۔ ایک تو وہ جس کے بدلے میں مدعی علیہ کے ہاتھ میں رقم وغیرہ آئی ہے جیسے بیع کی قیمت کا دعوی ہو تو مدعی علیہ کے ہاتھ میں مبیع آئی ہے جس کی قیمت ادا کرنی ہے یا مہر اس کے بدلے میں بضعہ آیا ہے۔ یا قرض کا مطالبہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کے ہاتھ میں قرض کی رقم آئی ہے۔ ان سب صورتوں میں مدعی کے ہاتھ میں مطالبے کا بدلہ آیا ہوا ہے پھر بھی وہ اس کا عوض نہیں دینا چاہتا۔ ایسی صورتوں میں مدعی علیہ غریب ہو یا مالدار اس کو جبس کیا جائے گا۔ اس کے ہاتھ میں بدل آنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ وہ عوض دے سکتا ہے تب ہی تو اس نے مثلا [بیع؟] خریدا، قرض لیا یا شادی کی (۲) اوپر جو حدیث گزری۔ (لى الواجد يحل عرضه وعقوبته ) اس میں فرمایا کہ مال پانے والے کے ٹال متول کی سزا یہ ہے کہ اس کی عزت بھی حلال ہے یعنی برا بھلا کہہ سکتے ہو اور اس کی سزا بھی حلال ہے یعنی [حبس؟] کر سکتے ہو۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال پانے والا ہو تو اس کو قید کر سکتے ہو۔ اور اگر ابھی فوری طور پر مال نہیں ملا ہے مثل کسی کا ہاتھ کا نا جس کی دیت ایک ہزار درہم دینے ہے تو ہاتھ کے بدلے میں قاطع کو بھی کچھ نہیں ملا ہے تو یہ ابھی مال کا پانے والا نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کو ابھی [حبس؟] نہیں کریں گے بلکہ تحقیق کے بعد معلوم ہو جائے کہ اس کے پاس [دیت؟] ادا کرنے کے لئے مال ہے پھر بھی ٹال مٹول کر رہا ہے تب [حبس؟] کریں گے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن جابر عن الشعبي قال: الحبس في الـديـن حـيـلـة قـال وقال جابر كان على يحبس في الدين (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الحبس فی الدین، ج ثامن، ص ۳۰۶ نمبر ۱۵۳۱۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ دین میں اور قرض میں [حبس؟] فرماتے تھے۔ اور اسی میں وہ تمام صورتیں داخل ہوں گی جس میں مدعی علیہ کو بدلہ مل گیا ہو۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علی دین میں قید کرتے تھے۔
A debt that becomes obligatory as a substitute for wealth that came into his hand, like the price of a sale and the substitute of a loan, or he obligated it by contract like the dowry and guarantee. When a right is proven against someone by witnesses, it means that the defendant was delaying for a long time. Finally the right was proven by witnesses, so if the judge wishes to imprison immediately, he may. Rights are of two types: one where the defendant has received a substitute, like the price of a sale, dowry, or loan. In these cases, the defendant has received a substitute, yet he does not want to pay. Whether rich or poor, he will be imprisoned. The fact that he received the substitute indicates he can pay. The hadith 'The evader of the wealthy man makes his honor and punishment permissible' indicates that one who has wealth can be imprisoned. If he has not yet received wealth, like a person whose hand is cut and owes diyah, then he has not received a substitute, so he will not be imprisoned immediately until his wealth is proven. The athar from Jabir and al-Sha'bi: 'Imprisonment for debt is a trick' and Ali used to imprison for debt. This includes all cases where the defendant received a substitute. Footnote: Ali used to imprison for debt.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on the etiquette of the judge. It explains that when the judge has proven a debt through witnesses, he may imprison the defendant if the defendant has received a substitute (badal) for the debt. The substitute is the wealth or benefit that came into the defendant's hands, such as the price of a sale, the loan amount, or the dowry. The key point is that receiving a substitute is itself an indication that the defendant has the ability to pay, as he would not have entered the transaction otherwise. The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'The evader of the wealthy man makes his honor and punishment permissible' supports this. The athar of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) confirms that he used to imprison for debt. The passage distinguishes between two types of rights: those where a substitute was received (allowing immediate imprisonment) and those where no substitute was received (like diyah for injury), where imprisonment is only allowed after proving the defendant's wealth. The footnote repeats that Ali imprisoned for debt.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute or equivalent; the wealth or benefit that comes into the defendant's hand in exchange for the debt.
الواجد (al-wajid): One who has wealth and is able to pay but evades payment.
حبس في الدين (habs fi al-dayn): Imprisonment for debt; a coercive measure by the judge to compel payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only if the defendant is poor
B) Only if the debt is from a sale
C) If the defendant has received a substitute for the debt

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment for debt is permissible when the debtor received a substitute (badal), as it indicates ability to pay; evidence from hadith and practice of Ali.

Imprisonment for Debt Without Substitute Requires Proof of Wealth
States the rule that defendant claiming poverty is not imprisoned unless creditor proves wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on imprisonment for debts where the defendant received no substitute (e.g., diyah), and apply the condition that the creditor must prove the defendant's wealth before imprisonment.

Core Idea
No imprisonment for a debtor claiming poverty until the creditor proves his wealth by evidence.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between debts where the defendant received a substitute (like a sale) and those where he did not (like diyah). In the latter, the default presumption is against imprisonment if the defendant claims poverty. This lesson examines the proof and condition for imprisonment in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of right
Determine whether the debt is one where the defendant received a substitute (e.g., price of sold goods) or not (e.g., diyah for injury). This lesson focuses on the latter.
The passage mentions 'diyah' as the example.
2
State the default rule
When the defendant says 'I am poor', the judge should not imprison him unless the creditor proves wealth.
The Arabic uses 'لا يحبسه' – prohibition of imprisonment.
3
Identify the condition for imprisonment
The only condition that allows imprisonment is the creditor providing witnesses to prove the defendant's wealth.
The text says 'الا ان يُثبت غريمه ان له مال' – unless his creditor proves he has wealth.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'لي الواجد يحل عرضه وعقوبته' restricts punishment (imprisonment) to the wealthy evader. Since the defendant claims poverty and has no substitute, he is not yet 'واجد' (wealthy), so imprisonment is not immediate.
Also the athar of Ali shows imprisonment only after proof.
5
Apply the ruling
In a case of diyah, if the creditor cannot prove the defendant's wealth, the judge must release the defendant or not imprison him at all.
This protects the poor debtor from wrongful imprisonment.

Source Text

٢٩٠٦ ( ۱۹ ) ولا يحبسه فيما سوى ذلك اذا قال انى فقير الا ان يُثبت غريمه ان له مال.  ایسے حقوق جس میں مدعی علیہ کے پاس اس کا بدل ہاتھ میں نہ آیا ہو جیسے جنایت کی دیت ، مثلا کسی کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا اس کے بدلے میں ایک ہزار درہم دیتا ہے تو اس صورت میں مجرم کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں آیا صرف جرم کی وجہ سے ایک ہزار درہم دینا پڑ رہا ہے۔ ایسی صورت میں اگر مدعی گواہ کے ذریعہ ثابت کر دے کہ اس کے پاس دیت ادا کرنے کے لئے مال ہے تب تو جبس کیا جائے گا۔ اور یہ ثابت نہ کر سکے تو جبس نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ چونکہ مدعی علیہ کے ہاتھ میں بدلے میں مال نہیں آیا ہے اس لئے اس کے مالدار ہونے کی دلیل نہیں ہے اس لئے فوری طور پر قید بھی نہیں کیا جائے گا (۲) اوپر حضرت علی کے اثر میں تھا اور حدیث میں بھی اشارہ تھا کہ دین کے بدلے میں جس کرتے تھے اس کے علاوہ میں مالدار ظاہر ہوئے بغیر میں نہیں کرتے تھے۔ وقال جابر كان على يحبس في الدين (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الحبس فی الدین، ج ثامن ص ۱۳۰۶، نمبر ۱۵۳۱۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دین میں جبس کرے۔ اور اوپر کی حدیث لی الواجد يحل عرضه وعقوبته (ب) : (ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی الدین هل تحبس به ، ج ۲، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۳۶۲۸) سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو مال پائے اس کی سزا حلال ہے یعنی قید کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ اور یہ چونکہ ابھی مال نہیں پا رہا ہے اس لئے فوری طور پر اس کو قید کرنا اچھا نہیں ہے جب تک گواہ کے ذریعہ اس کی مالداری ثابت نہ ہو جائے۔
And he should not imprison him in other than that when he says 'I am poor', unless his creditor proves that he has wealth. Such rights where the defendant has not received a substitute, like diyah for injury: for example, if someone's hand is cut, he owes a thousand dirhams as diyah, but the criminal has not received anything in return. In such a case, if the creditor proves by witnesses that he has wealth to pay the diyah, then he will be imprisoned; otherwise not. Since the defendant has not received a substitute, there is no indication of his wealth, so he will not be imprisoned immediately. The athar of Ali and the hadith indicate that imprisonment was for debt where a substitute was received; otherwise, not without proof of wealth. The hadith 'the evader of the wealthy man makes his honor and punishment permissible' shows that one who has wealth can be imprisoned, but this person has not yet received wealth, so immediate imprisonment is not good until his wealth is proven by witnesses.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof that clarifies the second type of right: where the defendant has not received any substitute for the debt. The example given is diyah (blood money) for a crime like cutting off a hand. The criminal owes diyah but has not received any wealth in exchange. In such cases, the defendant may claim poverty ('I am poor'). The judge should not imprison him unless the creditor proves by witnesses that the defendant actually has wealth. The reason is that there is no inherent indicator of solvency like in the first type. The athar of Ali and the hadith about the evader are again cited to show that immediate imprisonment is only for those who have received a substitute. The passage emphasizes the importance of proof of wealth before imprisonment in these cases.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money; compensation paid for injury or death, which becomes a debt without the defendant receiving a substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in a case of diyah, when can the judge imprison the defendant?
A) Immediately after the claim is proven
B) Only if the defendant is rich
C) Only if the creditor proves the defendant has wealth
D) Only if the defendant admits the debt

Key Takeaway
For debts without substitute, a debtor claiming poverty cannot be imprisoned until the creditor proves wealth; the burden of proof is on the creditor.

Qada — Judiciary
beginner
6 min
Maximum Imprisonment Period for Debtor
Specifies the maximum imprisonment period before inquiry and possible release

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum imprisonment period for a debtor in Hanafi law and identify the procedural steps following that period.

Core Idea
Imprisonment for debt is limited to a maximum of three months, after which release is mandatory if no wealth appears.

This lesson addresses a practical aspect of judicial procedure (qada): the duration of imprisonment for a debtor. The Hanafi school sets a clear limit to prevent indefinite detention while allowing the judge flexibility to investigate the debtor's financial situation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the judge's authority to imprison the debtor for two to three months. This is the maximum period under normal circumstances.
The judge has discretion within this range based on the case.
2
Identify the next procedural step
After the imprisonment period, the judge must inquire about the debtor's wealth. This is an obligation (wajib).
Inquiry ensures that the debtor is not held if he is truly insolvent.
3
Identify the consequence
If no wealth is found after inquiry, the judge must release the debtor immediately.
Release is mandatory (wajib) – continued detention becomes unlawful.
4
Understand the rationale
The limit prevents indefinite detention. The practice is based on the precedent of Ali (through his rulings on debt) and the hadith about the wealthy evader whose honor and punishment are permissible.
The footnote in the source highlights these evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۰۷] (۲۰) ويحبسه شهرين او ثلثة ثم يسأل عنه فان لم يظهر له مال خلى سبيله.  قید کی مدت حالات اور آدمی کے حسب حال ہے۔ البتہ اندازہ نہ ہو تو دو تین ماہ جبس کرے۔ اس کے درمیان میں اس کے مال کی تحقیق حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علی مقرض میں قید کرتے تھے (ب) جس کے پاس مال ہے اس کے ٹال مٹول کرنے والے کی عزت اور سزا بھی حلال ہے۔
And he should imprison him for two or three months, then inquire about him; if no wealth appears, he should release him. The duration of imprisonment is according to circumstances and the person. However, if there is no estimate, he should imprison for two or three months. During that time, investigate his wealth. Footnote: (a) Ali used to imprison for debt. (b) The evader of the wealthy man makes his honor and punishment permissible.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage provides a procedural ruling on the duration of imprisonment for debt. The judge may imprison the defendant for two to three months, after which he must inquire about the defendant's wealth. If no wealth is discovered, the defendant is to be released. The commentary adds that the duration can vary based on circumstances, but if no specific estimate is available, two to three months is the guideline. The footnote reiterates the principles from earlier: Ali's practice and the hadith about the wealthy evader. This ruling ensures that imprisonment is not indefinite and that the defendant is not held without cause.

Key Terms
خلى سبيله (khalla sabilahu): Release him; set him free from imprisonment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a judge do if no wealth appears after imprisoning a debtor for two to three months?
A) Continue imprisonment indefinitely
B) Release him
C) Increase the sentence
D) Fine him

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment for debt is limited to a maximum of three months, after which the judge must release the debtor if no wealth is found.
